     → O que não te mata te fortalece.

944. I came out stronger.
     → Saí mais forte.

945. It shaped who I am.
     → Moldou quem eu sou.

946. I wouldn't change a thing.
     → Não mudaria nada.

947. Everything led me here.
     → Tudo me trouxe até aqui.

948. I'm exactly where I'm supposed to be.
     → Estou exatamente onde deveria estar.

949. Things have a way of working out.
     → As coisas têm um jeito de se resolver.

950. Trust the process.
     → Confie no processo.

951. Good things take time.
     → Coisas boas levam tempo.

952. Rome wasn't built in a day.
     → Roma não foi construída em um dia.

953. Slow and steady wins the race.
     → Devagar e sempre se chega lá.

954. Patience is a virtue.
     → Paciência é uma virtude.

955. Good things come to those who wait.
     → As boas coisas vêm para quem espera.

956. But you also have to make things happen.
     → Mas você também tem que fazer as coisas acontecerem.

957. You can't just wait for luck.
     → Você não pode só esperar pela sorte.

958. Create your own luck.
     → Crie sua própria sorte.

959. Opportunity doesn't knock twice.
     → A oportunidade não bate duas vezes.

960. Seize the day.
     → Aproveite o dia.

961. YOLO — You only live once.
     → Você só vive uma vez.

962. Make it count.
     → Faça valer.

963. Leave a mark.
     → Deixe sua marca.

964. Make a difference.
     → Faça a diferença.

965. Be the change you want to see.
     → Seja a mudança que quer ver.

966. Lead by example.
     → Lidere pelo exemplo.

967. Actions speak louder than words.
     → Ações falam mais alto que palavras.

968. Put your money where your mouth is.
     → Prove com ações o que diz com palavras.

969. Walk the talk.
     → Faça o que fala.

970. Practice what you preach.
     → Pratique o que prega.

971. Mean what you say.
     → Diga o que quer dizer.

972. Say what you mean.
     → Queira dizer o que diz.

973. Be direct. / Get to the point.
     → Seja direto. / Vá ao ponto.

974. Don't beat around the bush.
     → Não rodeie o assunto.
     MACETE: "beat around the bush" = ficar enrolando sem chegar ao ponto

975. I'll be straight with you.
     → Serei direto com você.

976. Let me be real with you.
     → Deixa eu ser honesto com você.

977. No sugarcoating.
     → Sem dourar a pílula.

978. The truth is...
     → A verdade é...

979. Whether you like it or not.
     → Quer você goste ou não.

980. That's the reality.
     → Essa é a realidade.

981. Face the facts.
     → Enfrente os fatos.

982. Get real.
     → Seja realista. / Acorde para a realidade.

983. Wake up.
     → Acorde. / Abra os olhos.

984. Read the room.
     → Leia o ambiente. / Leia a situação.
     MACETE: "read the room" = entender o clima/ambiente social

985. Know your audience.
     → Conheça seu público.

986. Pick your battles.
     → Escolha suas batalhas.

987. Not every battle is worth fighting.
     → Nem toda batalha vale a pena lutar.

988. Let the small things go.
     → Deixa as pequenas coisas irem.

989. Focus on what matters.
     → Foque no que importa.

990. Keep your eyes on the prize.
     → Mantenha os olhos no prêmio.

991. Stay focused. / Stay on track.
     → Mantenha o foco. / Mantenha-se no caminho.

992. Don't get distracted.
     → Não se distraia.

993. You're almost there. Keep going.
     → Você está quase lá. Continue.

994. Don't stop now.
     → Não pare agora.

995. The finish line is in sight.
     → A linha de chegada está à vista.

996. Give it everything you've got.
     → Dê tudo o que tem.

997. This is your moment.
     → Esse é o seu momento.

998. You were made for this.
     → Você foi feito para isso.

999. Now go out there and show them what you've got.
     → Agora vai lá e mostra do que você é capaz.

1000. The world is yours.
      → O mundo é seu.

PILAR 4 — 150 TEXTOS COM CONTEXTO VISUAL

Do básico ao avançado · Agrupados por tema

BLOCO A — TRABALHO (textos 1–25)

TEXTO 01 — "Monday Morning" | Nível: Iniciante
Tom wakes up at 7am. He is tired.
He goes to the kitchen and makes coffee.
The coffee is hot. Tom drinks it slowly.
He looks at the window. It is raining outside.
"Not a great Monday," he thinks.
He gets his bag and goes to work anyway.
VOCABULÁRIO: wakes up · tired · kitchen · slowly · raining · anyway
PERGUNTA: Why does Tom think it's not a great Monday?
CENA: personagem na cozinha, chuva na janela, xícara fumegando

TEXTO 02 — "The Email" | Nível: Iniciante
Sarah sits at her desk. She opens her computer.
She has 47 new emails. She sighs.
"Too many emails," she says.
She starts with the most important one.
It's from her boss. He wants a report by noon.
Sarah looks at the clock. It's 10am. She has two hours.
"I can do this," she says. She starts writing.
VOCABULÁRIO: desk · opens · sighs · important · report · noon · clock
PERGUNTA: How much time does Sarah have to write the report?
CENA: personagem no computador, caixa de entrada cheia, relógio

TEXTO 03 — "The Meeting" | Nível: Iniciante
The meeting starts at 2pm. Everyone sits down.
The manager speaks first. He talks for a long time.
Some people are bored. One man falls asleep.
Then someone asks a question. The room wakes up.
At 3:30, the meeting ends. People are relieved.
"Finally!" says one woman. They all laugh.
VOCABULÁRIO: meeting · manager · bored · falls asleep · relieved · finally
PERGUNTA: What time does the meeting end?
CENA: sala de reunião, pessoas em volta da mesa, um adormecido

TEXTO 04 — "Lunch Break" | Nível: Iniciante
It's noon. Time for lunch.
Carlos goes to the restaurant near his office.
He orders a sandwich and a juice.
He sits alone and checks his phone.
He has a message from his wife: "How's your day?"
He smiles and writes back: "Busy. But okay."
He finishes his lunch and goes back to work.
VOCABULÁRIO: noon · orders · sandwich · checks · message · smiles · writes back
PERGUNTA: Who sends Carlos a message?
CENA: restaurante simples, personagem sozinho com sanduíche e celular

TEXTO 05 — "Working Late" | Nível: Intermediário
It's 7pm and the office is almost empty.
Ana is still at her desk. She has a deadline tomorrow.
She's been working on this project for three weeks.
Her eyes are tired. Her coffee is cold.
She thinks about going home, but the work isn't done.
She takes a deep breath and keeps typing.
An hour later, she finishes. She packs her bag.
Walking out, she feels exhausted but proud.
VOCABULÁRIO: deadline · project · exhausted · proud · packs · keeps typing · deep breath
PERGUNTA: How long has Ana been working on the project?
CENA: escritório vazio à noite, uma luz acesa, personagem sozinha

TEXTO 06 — "The Job Interview" | Nível: Intermediário
David is nervous. Today is his job interview.
He arrives 10 minutes early. Good sign.
He wears his best shirt. His hands are shaking a little.
The interviewer comes in. She shakes his hand firmly.
"Tell me about yourself," she says.
David takes a breath and begins. He prepared for this.
The interview goes well. At the end, she smiles.
"We'll be in touch," she says. He leaves feeling hopeful.
VOCABULÁRIO: nervous · arrives · shaking · interviewer · firmly · prepared · hopeful · be in touch
PERGUNTA: Why does David feel hopeful at the end?

TEXTO 07 — "Remote Work Day" | Nível: Intermediário
Laura works from home today. She loves remote days.
No commute. No office noise. Just her and her computer.
She makes breakfast properly — scrambled eggs and toast.
She starts work at 9am, focused and comfortable.
But by 2pm, she misses her coworkers.
She sends them a funny meme in the group chat.
They all react with laughing emojis.
She smiles. Remote work has its ups and downs.
VOCABULÁRIO: commute · scrambled · focused · coworkers · meme · react · ups and downs
PERGUNTA: What does Laura miss about the office?

TEXTO 08 — "The Promotion" | Nível: Intermediário
Mark has been at this company for four years.
He works hard. He never misses a deadline.
Today, his manager calls him into the office.
Mark's heart beats faster. Did he do something wrong?
"Mark," says the manager, "we're promoting you."
Mark blinks. He didn't expect this. "Thank you," he says.
Walking back to his desk, he can't stop smiling.
He calls his wife. "You won't believe what just happened."
VOCABULÁRIO: promoting · blinks · expect · deadline · beating · believe
PERGUNTA: How did Mark feel when his manager called him in?

TEXTO 09 — "Difficult Coworker" | Nível: Intermediário
Everyone in the office likes each other. Except Paulo.
Paulo talks too loud. He never listens in meetings.
He always takes credit for other people's work.
Today he did it again. He presented Linda's idea as his own.
Linda was furious, but she said nothing in the meeting.
Later, she went to her manager and explained everything.
The manager nodded. "I know," he said. "I've noticed."
Linda felt better. Sometimes patience pays off.
VOCABULÁRIO: credit · presented · furious · explained · nodded · noticed · patience · pays off
PERGUNTA: What does Paulo do that is unfair?

TEXTO 10 — "End of the Year" | Nível: Avançado
It was the last working day of the year.
The team gathered in the conference room.
Someone brought a cake. Another brought sparkling water.
The manager made a short speech about the year's challenges.
He mentioned the project that almost failed — and then didn't.
He talked about the new clients, the long nights, the setbacks.
"But we made it," he said. "Together."
Everyone raised their glasses. Someone started clapping.
It wasn't a perfect year. But it was theirs.
VOCABULÁRIO: gathered · sparkling · speech · challenges · setbacks · raised · clapping · theirs
PERGUNTA: What does the manager say about the difficult project?

BLOCO B — COMPRAS (textos 26–50)

TEXTO 26 — "At the Market" | Nível: Iniciante
Maria goes to the market every Saturday.
She buys fruits, vegetables, and bread.
Today she sees a new fruit. It's called a persimmon.
She asks the vendor: "Is it sweet?"
"Very sweet," he says. "Try one."
She tries it. She loves it. She buys three.
VOCABULÁRIO: market · buys · persimmon · vendor · sweet · tries
PERGUNTA: What does Maria try for the first time?
CENA: banca de frutas coloridas, personagem experimentando fruta

TEXTO 27 — "Too Expensive" | Nível: Iniciante
Ben is at the shoe store. He needs new shoes.
He finds a pair he loves. He looks at the price.
$180. That's too expensive.
He puts them back. He looks for something cheaper.
He finds another pair. $45. Not as beautiful, but okay.
He buys them. He's not completely happy, but his wallet is.
VOCABULÁRIO: pair · expensive · cheaper · completely · wallet
PERGUNTA: Why doesn't Ben buy the first pair of shoes?
CENA: loja de sapatos, personagem olhando preço com choque

TEXTO 28 — "Online Shopping at 2am" | Nível: Iniciante
It's 2am. Everyone is asleep. Except Lucas.
Lucas is on his phone, shopping online.
He doesn't need anything. But everything looks good.
He adds a jacket to his cart. Then a book. Then a lamp.
His total is $200. He stares at the screen.
He removes the lamp. Still $160.
He closes the app. He puts his phone down.
He opens the app again. He buys the jacket.
VOCABULÁRIO: cart · total · stares · removes · closes · buys
PERGUNTA: What does Lucas buy in the end?
CENA: quarto escuro, pessoa iluminada pelo celular, 2am no relógio

TEXTO 29 — "The Return" | Nível: Intermediário
Sandra bought a dress last week. It doesn't fit.
Today she goes back to the store to return it.
She explains the situation to the cashier.
"Do you have the receipt?" the cashier asks.
Sandra searches her bag. She can't find it.
She searches again. There it is, at the bottom.
The cashier processes the return. Sandra gets her money back.
"Always keep your receipts," she tells herself on the way out.
VOCABULÁRIO: return · fit · receipt · searches · processes · bottom · keep
PERGUNTA: What problem does Sandra have at first?

TEXTO 30 — "Black Friday" | Nível: Intermediário
It's 6am on Black Friday. The mall opens at 7.
Outside, there's already a long line.
People hold coffee cups and look at their phones.
They're all waiting for the same thing: the deals.
When the doors open, everyone moves fast.
It's loud, chaotic, and exciting all at once.
By noon, most of the best deals are gone.
But many people walk out happy, bags in both hands.
VOCABULÁRIO: mall · line · deals · chaotic · exciting · noon · walk out
PERGUNTA: What happens when the mall opens?

BLOCO C — FAMÍLIA (textos 51–75)

TEXTO 51 — "Sunday Lunch" | Nível: Iniciante
Every Sunday, the family has lunch together.
Grandma cooks. It always smells amazing.
The table is full of food. Everyone eats a lot.
The kids run around after the meal.
The adults talk and drink coffee.
At 5pm, everyone starts to leave.
Hugs. Kisses. See you next Sunday.
VOCABULÁRIO: together · smells · meal · adults · hugs · kisses
PERGUNTA: What do the adults do after the meal?
CENA: mesa de almoço cheia, família reunida, avó trazendo comida

TEXTO 52 — "The First Day of School" | Nível: Iniciante
Today is the first day of school for little Emma.
She's five years old. She has a new backpack.
Her mom holds her hand as they walk in.
Emma sees other kids. She feels shy.
But then a girl smiles at her. "I'm Lily," she says.
Emma smiles back. "I'm Emma."
By the end of the day, they're already friends.
VOCABULÁRIO: backpack · holds · shy · smiles · already · friends
PERGUNTA: How does Emma feel at first?
CENA: entrada da escola, criança com mochila nova, outra criança sorrindo

TEXTO 53 — "The Phone Call" | Nível: Iniciante
Rafael calls his mother every Sunday.
They talk for about an hour.
She tells him about her week. He listens.
He tells her about his work. She listens.
Sometimes they don't have much to say.
But they stay on the phone anyway.
That's how love sounds sometimes — like comfortable silence.
VOCABULÁRIO: calls · hour · tells · listens · comfortable · silence
PERGUNTA: How long do Rafael and his mother usually talk?
CENA: homem adulto no sofá com celular, sorrindo, ambiente noturno

TEXTO 54 — "Growing Up Too Fast" | Nível: Intermediário
Maya looks at her son's old photos. He was so small.
In the photos, he fits in her arms completely.
Now he's 15. Almost as tall as her husband.
He has his own music. His own opinions. His own world.
She knocks on his door: "Can I come in?"
He looks up from his phone. "Sure, Mom."
They talk for a while. About nothing important.
But for Maya, these small moments are everything.
VOCABULÁRIO: fits · completely · opinions · knocks · looks up · moments
PERGUNTA: How old is Maya's son now?

TEXTO 55 — "The Argument" | Nível: Intermediário
Ana and her sister had a fight last month.
It was over something small. Now neither remembers what.
But the silence has lasted four weeks.
Today, Ana picks up her phone. She dials her sister's number.
It rings twice. Then: "Hello?"
Ana's voice shakes a little. "Hi. I miss you."
Silence. Then: "I miss you too."
They talk for two hours. The argument is forgotten.
VOCABULÁRIO: argument · silence · lasted · picks up · dials · shakes · forgotten
PERGUNTA: Who makes the first move to end the silence?

BLOCO D — ROTINA (textos 76–100)

TEXTO 76 — "The Alarm" | Nível: Iniciante
The alarm rings at 6am. Pedro hits snooze.
It rings again at 6:10. He hits snooze again.
At 6:20, he finally gets up.
He's late. He knows it. He rushes to the bathroom.
No time for breakfast. He grabs a banana.
He runs to the bus stop. The bus is just leaving.
He catches it. Just in time. He breathes. He made it.
VOCABULÁRIO: alarm · snooze · rushes · grabs · catches · just in time · breathes
PERGUNTA: Does Pedro make it to the bus?
CENA: despertador tocando, personagem dormindo, ônibus saindo

TEXTO 77 — "Evening Routine" | Nível: Iniciante
After work, Julia always does the same things.
She changes her clothes. She makes tea.
She sits on the sofa and watches something light.
A comedy. A cooking show. Something relaxing.
At 10pm, she reads for 30 minutes.
Then she turns off the light. She's asleep in minutes.
Her routine is simple. But it makes her happy.
VOCABULÁRIO: changes · tea · sofa · comedy · relaxing · routine · asleep
PERGUNTA: What does Julia do before sleeping?

TEXTO 78 — "The Gym" | Nível: Intermediário
It's 6am and the gym is already busy.
People lift weights. People run on treadmills.
In the corner, Carlos is doing push-ups.
He comes here every morning. It wasn't always like this.
A year ago, he could barely do five.
Now he does fifty without stopping.
He remembers when getting up at 6am felt impossible.
Now it just feels like Tuesday.
VOCABULÁRIO: lift · treadmills · push-ups · barely · stopping · impossible · Tuesday
PERGUNTA: How many push-ups can Carlos do now compared to a year ago?

BLOCO E — EMOÇÕES E SITUAÇÕES (textos 101–150)

TEXTO 101 — "The Good News" | Nível: Iniciante
Carla gets a message. She reads it twice.
She got the job. The one she really wanted.
She stares at the screen. She can't believe it.
Then she screams. Then she laughs.
She calls her mom. Her mom cries.
"I'm so proud of you," her mom says.
Carla cries too. Happy tears.
VOCABULÁRIO: message · got · stares · screams · cries · proud · tears
PERGUNTA: How does Carla feel when she gets the message?
CENA: personagem gritando de alegria com celular na mão

TEXTO 102 — "The Bad Day" | Nível: Iniciante
Everything went wrong today.
First, it rained and Ricardo forgot his umbrella.
Then he spilled coffee on his shirt.
In the meeting, he forgot his presentation.
He missed lunch because of a call.
He got home late, wet and hungry.
He sat on the sofa and sighed.
Then his dog came and sat on his lap. And he felt better.
VOCABULÁRIO: forgot · spilled · missed · wet · hungry · sighed · lap · better
PERGUNTA: What makes Ricardo feel better in the end?
CENA: homem no sofá, cachorro no colo, expressão de alívio

TEXTO 103 — "The Apology" | Nível: Intermediário
They hadn't spoken in three days.
It started with a small argument that got bigger.
Both thought the other should apologize first.
On the third day, he knocked on the bedroom door.
"Can we talk?" he asked.
She opened it. "I was going to knock first," she said.
They both laughed. The tension broke.
They talked for an hour. They went to bed holding hands.
Some problems aren't solved — they're softened by love.
VOCABULÁRIO: spoken · argument · apologize · knocked · tension · broke · softened
PERGUNTA: Who apologizes first?

TEXTO 104 — "Starting Over" | Nível: Avançado
At 42, Fernanda decided to go back to university.
Everyone thought she was crazy. She thought so too, sometimes.
She sat in classrooms full of 20-year-olds, her notebook open.
In the beginning, she felt out of place. Invisible. Old.
But she raised her hand one day. She answered correctly.
The professor nodded. A student next to her smiled.
"Good answer," the student said.
That was the day she stopped feeling like she didn't belong.
Two years later, she graduated. Her daughter cheered from the crowd.
VOCABULÁRIO: decided · classrooms · invisible · raised · correctly · belong · graduated · cheered
PERGUNTA: What moment made Fernanda feel like she belonged?

TEXTO 105 — "The Last Day" | Nível: Avançado
It was her last day at the company. Fifteen years.
She had packed her desk into two cardboard boxes.
A plant. Some photos. A mug that said "Boss."
Her team gathered around her desk at 5pm.
They gave her a card signed by everyone. And a gift.
She opened it: a journal with a note inside.
"For the next chapter," it said.
She cried a little. Then laughed. Then hugged everyone.
Walking out for the last time, she didn't look back.
The next chapter was already waiting.
VOCABULÁRIO: packed · cardboard · gathered · signed · journal · chapter · hugged · waiting
PERGUNTA: What does the note in the gift say?

SISTEMA 5 — FRASES RELÂMPAGO

Shadowing: ouça, repita, grave na memória

Baseado em: "Domine Estas 150 Frases Curtas em Inglês"

O QUE É SHADOWING

Shadowing = você vê a frase em português, tenta dizer em inglês
antes de ver a resposta, depois repete em voz alta 3 vezes.

É a técnica mais eficaz para desenvolver fluência automática —
você para de "traduzir na cabeça" e começa a falar diretamente.

COMO USAR ESTE SISTEMA:

  1. Veja a frase em português
  2. Tente dizer em inglês em voz alta (sem ver a resposta)
  3. Veja a frase em inglês
  4. Repita 3 vezes em voz alta
  5. Avance para a próxima

AS 150 FRASES — 10 GRUPOS DE 15

GRUPO 1 — ESTADOS (I'm feeling... / I feel...)

Como você está agora — 15 frases

01. Estou me sentindo pronto.      → I feel ready.
02. Estou me sentindo ótimo.       → I'm feeling great.
03. Estou me sentindo calmo.       → I'm feeling calm.
04. Estou me sentindo forte.       → I'm feeling strong.
05. Estou me sentindo cansado.     → I'm feeling tired.
06. Estou me sentindo bem.         → I'm feeling good.
07. Estou me sentindo melhor.      → I'm feeling better.
08. Estou me sentindo pronto agora.→ I feel ready now.
09. Estou bem.                     → I'm doing fine.
10. Estou indo bem.                → I'm doing okay.
11. Estou melhorando.              → I'm doing better.
12. Estou fazendo o meu melhor.    → I'm doing my best.
13. Ainda não estou pronto.        → I'm not ready yet.
14. Estou quase pronto.            → I'm almost ready.
15. Estou me sentindo confiante.   → I'm feeling confident.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • I feel + [adjetivo] → estado permanente ou mais formal
  • I'm feeling + [adjetivo] → estado no momento atual
  • I'm doing + [adjetivo/advérbio] → como você está se saindo

MACETE:
"How are you?" → "I'm doing great!" (não apenas "I'm great")
"I'm doing" soa mais natural e fluente.

GRUPO 2 — MOVIMENTO (I'm going... / I'm leaving... / I'm coming...)

Onde você está indo — 15 frases

16. Acordei cedo.                  → I woke up early.
17. Estou saindo.                  → I'm going outside.
18. Estou ficando dentro.          → I'm staying inside.
19. Estou saindo agora.            → I'm leaving now.
20. Estou chegando em breve.       → I'm coming soon.
21. Estou atrasado.                → I'm running late.
22. Estou a caminho.               → I'm on my way.
23. Estou voltando.                → I'm coming back.
24. Estou indo para casa.          → I'm heading home.
25. Estou quase lá.                → I'm almost there.
26. Preciso me apressar.           → I need to hurry.
27. Estou indo agora.              → I'm leaving now.
28. Estou chegando.                → I'm on my way.
29. Estou ficando aqui.            → I'm staying here.
30. Estou indo embora.             → I'm going away.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • I'm going/leaving/coming/staying + [complemento]
  • "Running late" = estar atrasado (não "being late")
  • "On my way" = a caminho (expressão idiomática muito usada)

MACETE:
"I'm running late" → literalmente "estou correndo atrasado"
É a expressão padrão americana para "estou atrasado"

GRUPO 3 — NECESSIDADES (I need...)

O que você precisa — 15 frases

31. Preciso de um minuto.          → I need a minute.
32. Preciso de descanso.           → I need some rest.
33. Preciso de mais tempo.         → I need more time.
34. Preciso me concentrar.         → I need to focus.
35. Preciso da sua ajuda.          → I need your help.
36. Preciso de uma pausa.          → I need a break.
37. Preciso de ar fresco.          → I need fresh air.
38. Preciso de espaço.             → I need some space.
39. Preciso pensar.                → I need to think.
40. Preciso relaxar.               → I need to relax.
41. Preciso dormir.                → I need to sleep.
42. Preciso comer.                 → I need to eat.
43. Preciso de água.               → I need some water.
44. Preciso sair daqui.            → I need to get out of here.
45. Preciso de uma solução.        → I need a solution.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • I need + [substantivo] → necessidade de algo
  • I need to + [verbo] → necessidade de fazer algo
  • "Some" antes de palavras incontáveis: some rest, some space, some water

MACETE:
"I need a break" = preciso de uma pausa (trabalho/estudo)
"I need some space" = preciso de espaço (emocional/físico)
O contexto muda o significado!

GRUPO 4 — DESEJOS (I want...)

O que você quer — 15 frases

46. Quero aprender.                → I want to learn.
47. Quero crescer.                 → I want to grow.
48. Quero melhorar.                → I want to improve.
49. Quero tentar.                  → I want to try.
50. Quero vencer.                  → I want to win.
51. Quero descansar.               → I want to rest.
52. Quero comer.                   → I want to eat.
53. Quero dormir.                  → I want to sleep.
54. Quero ir.                      → I want to go.
55. Quero ficar.                   → I want to stay.
56. Quero entender.                → I want to understand.
57. Quero tentar de novo.          → I want to try again.
58. Quero fazer melhor.            → I want to do better.
59. Quero saber mais.              → I want to know more.
60. Quero mudar.                   → I want to change.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • I want to + [verbo base]
  • Mais educado: "I'd like to + [verbo]"
  • Ainda mais educado: "I'd love to + [verbo]"

MACETE:
I want to → quero (direto)
I'd like to → gostaria de (educado)
I'd love to → adoraria (entusiasmado)

GRUPO 5 — POSSESSIVOS (I have...)

O que você tem — 15 frases

61. Eu tenho um plano.             → I have a plan.
62. Eu tenho uma ideia.            → I have an idea.
63. Eu tenho uma pergunta.         → I have a question.
64. Eu tenho algum tempo.          → I have some time.
65. Eu tenho um problema.          → I have a problem.
66. Eu tenho uma solução.          → I have a solution.
67. Eu tenho uma chance.           → I have a chance.
68. Eu tenho um objetivo.          → I have a goal.
69. Eu tenho energia.              → I have energy.
70. Eu tenho esperança.            → I have hope.
71. Eu tenho uma dúvida.           → I have a doubt.
72. Eu tenho uma sugestão.         → I have a suggestion.
73. Eu tenho uma promessa.         → I have a promise.
74. Eu tenho um recado.            → I have a message.
75. Eu tenho uma notícia.          → I have some news.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • I have + a/an + [substantivo contável singular]
  • I have + some + [substantivo incontável]
  • MACETE: "I have an idea!" → sempre com "an" antes de vogal

ERRO CLÁSSICO DO BRASILEIRO:
❌ "I have a news" → news é incontável!
✓ "I have some news" / "I have a piece of news"

GRUPO 6 — OBSERVAÇÕES IT (It looks/sounds/feels/seems...)

Como algo parece — 15 frases

76.  Parece bom.                   → It looks good.
77.  Soa bem.                      → It sounds nice.
78.  Parece certo.                 → It feels right.
79.  Parece fácil.                 → It seems easy.
80.  Parece difícil.               → It seems hard.
81.  Parece melhor.                → It looks better.
82.  Soa ótimo.                    → It sounds great.
83.  Parece estranho.              → It seems strange.
84.  Parece claro.                 → It's clear.
85.  Parece simples.               → It looks simple.
86.  Parece perfeito.              → It looks perfect.
87.  Soa familiar.                 → It sounds familiar.
88.  Parece importante.            → It seems important.
89.  Parece interessante.          → It looks interesting.
90.  Soa correto.                  → It sounds right.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO — OS 4 SENTIDOS:

  • It looks = parece (visualmente)
  • It sounds = soa / parece (auditivamente ou por informação)
  • It feels = parece (sensação / intuição)
  • It seems = parece (opinião / impressão geral)

MACETE VISUAL:

OLHOS  → looks  → "It looks good" (você vê)
OUVIDOS→ sounds → "It sounds nice" (você ouve ou ouviu falar)
TOQUE  → feels  → "It feels right" (você sente / intuição)
MENTE  → seems  → "It seems hard" (você acha / impressão)

GRUPO 7 — ISSO/THIS (This is... / This feels...)

Falando de algo próximo — 15 frases

91.  Isso parece bom.              → This feels good.
92.  Isso parece bonito.           → This looks beautiful.
93.  Isso soa ótimo.               → This sounds great.
94.  Isso parece certo.            → This feels right.
95.  Isso funciona bem.            → This works well.
96.  Isso me ajuda.                → This helps me.
97.  Isso é suficiente.            → This is enough.
98.  Isso é perfeito.              → This is perfect.
99.  Isso é melhor.                → This is better.
100. Isso é simples.               → This is simple.
101. Isso é diferente.             → This is different.
102. Isso faz sentido.             → This makes sense.
103. Isso é o que eu quero.        → This is what I want.
104. Isso é incrível.              → This is amazing.
105. Isso muda tudo.               → This changes everything.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • This = isso/este (perto de você, específico)
  • That = aquilo/aquele (longe de você ou já mencionado)
  • "This is what I want" → This como sujeito complexo

MACETE:
This = aqui perto, agora
That = lá longe, antes, ou abstrato

"This coffee is great." (o café que está na minha mão)
"That coffee we had yesterday was great." (o de ontem)

GRUPO 8 — AQUILO/THAT (That is... / That feels...)

Falando de algo distante — 15 frases

106. Aquilo parece bom.            → That feels good.
107. Aquilo parece bonito.         → That looks beautiful.
108. Aquilo soa ótimo.             → That sounds great.
109. Aquilo parece certo.          → That feels right.
110. Aquilo funciona bem.          → That works well.
111. Aquilo me ajuda.              → That helps me.
112. Aquilo é suficiente.          → That is enough.
113. Aquilo é perfeito.            → That is perfect.
114. Aquilo é melhor.              → That is better.
115. Aquilo é simples.             → That is simple.
116. Aquilo foi incrível.          → That was amazing.
117. Aquilo faz sentido.           → That makes sense.
118. Aquilo é o que eu quero.      → That's what I want.
119. Aquilo mudou tudo.            → That changed everything.
120. Aquilo foi perfeito.          → That was perfect.

COMPARAÇÃO THIS vs THAT:

This is good.  → Isso (na sua mão) é bom.
That is good.  → Aquilo (lá) é bom.
That was good. → Aquilo foi bom. (passado)
That sounds good. → Isso parece bom. (sobre ideia/plano)

MACETE:
"That sounds good!" → usado para concordar com planos
"That makes sense!" → usado para confirmar compreensão
"That's what I want!" → ênfase no desejo

GRUPO 9 — VAMOS (Let's...)

Convidando para ação — 15 frases

121. Vamos tentar novamente.       → Let's try again.
122. Vamos começar agora.          → Let's start now.
123. Vamos seguir em frente.       → Let's move on.
124. Vamos embora agora.           → Let's go now.
125. Vamos continuar.              → Let's keep going.
126. Vamos manter a calma.         → Let's stay calm.
127. Vamos manter o foco.          → Let's stay focused.
128. Vamos fazer uma pausa.        → Let's take a break.
129. Vamos terminar isto.          → Let's finish this.
130. Vamos fazer melhor.           → Let's do better.
131. Vamos trabalhar juntos.       → Let's work together.
132. Vamos pensar nisso.           → Let's think about this.
133. Vamos resolver isso.          → Let's figure this out.
134. Vamos ser honestos.           → Let's be honest.
135. Vamos aproveitar.             → Let's enjoy this.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • Let's + [verbo base] = vamos + [verbo]
  • Let's = Let us (forma contraída)
  • Sempre seguido de verbo NO INFINITIVO SEM "to"

ERRO CLÁSSICO:
❌ "Let's to go" → ✓ "Let's go"
❌ "Let's to try" → ✓ "Let's try"

EXPRESSÕES ESPECIAIS:

  • "Let's move on" = vamos seguir / passar para o próximo assunto
  • "Let's keep going" = vamos continuar / não pare
  • "Let's figure this out" = vamos resolver isso / descobrir

GRUPO 10 — VOU/COMPROMISSO (I will...)

Suas intenções e compromissos — 15 frases

136. Vou tentar novamente.         → I will try again.
137. Vou começar agora.            → I will start now.
138. Vou continuar.                → I will keep going.
139. Vou manter a calma.           → I will stay calm.
140. Vou manter o foco.            → I will stay focused.
141. Vou fazer uma pausa.          → I will take a break.
142. Vou terminar isto.            → I will finish this.
143. Vou fazer melhor.             → I will do better.
144. Vou aprender mais.            → I will learn more.
145. Vou voltar.                   → I will come back.
146. Vou resolver isso.            → I will figure this out.
147. Vou me esforçar mais.         → I will try harder.
148. Vou ser mais cuidadoso.       → I will be more careful.
149. Vou fazer isso hoje.          → I will do this today.
150. Vou dar o meu melhor.         → I will give my best.

PADRÃO DO GRUPO:

  • I will + [verbo base] = decisão / promessa / intenção
  • Forma contraída: I'll (muito mais natural na fala)
  • "I'll try again" soa mais natural que "I will try again"

WILL vs GOING TO:

  • I will = decisão no momento / promessa
  • I'm going to = plano já feito

"Oh, the phone's ringing — I'll get it!" (decisão agora)
"I'm going to call you tomorrow." (plano já feito)

RESUMO VISUAL DOS 10 PADRÕES

GRUPO 1:  I feel / I'm feeling      → como você está
GRUPO 2:  I'm going / I'm leaving   → onde você vai
GRUPO 3:  I need                    → o que você precisa
GRUPO 4:  I want to                 → o que você quer
GRUPO 5:  I have                    → o que você tem
GRUPO 6:  It looks/sounds/feels     → como algo parece
GRUPO 7:  This is / This feels      → isso (próximo)
GRUPO 8:  That is / That was        → aquilo (distante)
GRUPO 9:  Let's                     → vamos (em grupo)
GRUPO 10: I will                    → vou (compromisso)

SISTEMA 6 — CONVERSAS DO DIA A DIA

Perguntas e respostas naturais sobre situações reais

Baseado em: "English Speaking Practice | Speak Like a Native"

AS 14 CONVERSAS — 7 Q&A CADA = 98 PARES

CONVERSA 01 — ROTINA DIÁRIA DE TRABALHO

Tema: Trabalho, horários, rotina
Nível: Iniciante
Question words: What / How / When

Q: What time do you get up?
A: I get up at around 6 a.m.

Q: How do you get to work?
A: I usually walk to work.

Q: When does your work day start?
A: It starts at 9:00 a.m.

Q: What do you do during lunch?
A: I eat at the office cafeteria.

Q: How long is your lunch break?
A: It's about 1 hour long.

Q: When do you finish work?
A: I finish at 5:00 p.m.

Q: What do you do in the evening?
A: I watch YouTube videos and relax.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • get up = acordar / levantar
  • walk to work = ir ao trabalho a pé
  • work day = dia de trabalho
  • lunch break = pausa para almoço
  • cafeteria = cantina / refeitório
  • in the evening = à noite / no período da tarde/noite

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "I get up at around ___." → Acordo por volta das ___.
  2. "I usually walk to ___." → Geralmente vou a pé para ___.
  3. "It starts at ___." → Começa às ___.
  4. "It's about ___ long." → Dura cerca de ___.

PRATIQUE FALANDO SOBRE VOCÊ:

  • What time do you get up? → I get up at ___.
  • How do you get to work/school? → I ___ to ___.
  • What do you do in the evening? → I ___.

ANÁLISE DE QUESTION WORDS:

  • WHAT = o quê / qual (objeto, atividade)
  • HOW = como (maneira, modo)
  • WHEN = quando (tempo)
  • HOW LONG = quanto tempo (duração)

CONVERSA 02 — CIDADE NATAL

Tema: Origem, cidade natal, saudades
Nível: Iniciante
Question words: Where / How / What / Do / Will

Q: Where are you from originally?
A: I'm from a small town in Mexico.

Q: How big is your hometown?
A: It has about 50,000 people.

Q: What is your hometown known for?
A: It's known for its colorful festivals.

Q: How is it different from this city?
A: It's much quieter and slower paced.

Q: What do people do there for fun?
A: They go to the plaza on weekends.

Q: Do you miss your hometown?
A: Yes, I miss it very much.

Q: Will you go back someday?
A: Yes, I hope to go back soon.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • originally = originalmente / de origem
  • hometown = cidade natal
  • known for = conhecido por / famoso por
  • slower paced = ritmo mais lento / pace mais tranquilo
  • plaza = praça / centro
  • miss = sentir falta de
  • someday = algum dia

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "I'm from a small town in ___." → Sou de uma cidade pequena em ___.
  2. "It's known for its ___." → É conhecida por seu/sua ___.
  3. "It's much quieter and slower paced." → É muito mais quieto e com ritmo mais lento.
  4. "I miss it very much." → Sinto muita falta.
  5. "I hope to go back soon." → Espero voltar em breve.

ERRO CLÁSSICO:
❌ "I miss my city." (correto mas incompleto)
✓ "I miss it very much." (mais natural — usa pronome)
✓ "I really miss my hometown." (mais expressivo)

PRATIQUE COM SUA PRÓPRIA HISTÓRIA:

  • Where are you from originally? → I'm from ___ in ___.
  • What is your hometown known for? → It's known for its ___.
  • Do you miss your hometown? → Yes, I miss ___ / Not really, because ___.

CONVERSA 03 — FILMES E CINEMA

Tema: Filmes, preferências, recomendações
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Question words: What / Why / Who / How often / Was / Would

Q: What kind of movies do you like?
A: I love thrillers and science fiction.

Q: Why do you like science fiction?
A: I love imagining life in the future.

Q: Who is your favorite actor?
A: I really like Cate Blanchett's work.

Q: How often do you go to the cinema?
A: I go about twice a month.

Q: What was the last movie you saw?
A: I saw an action film last weekend.

Q: Was it good?
A: It was okay. Not the best.

Q: What would you recommend watching?
A: You should watch that new Spanish series.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • thrillers = filmes de suspense
  • science fiction = ficção científica
  • imagining = imaginando
  • favorite actor = ator favorito
  • cinema = cinema (o local)
  • action film = filme de ação
  • recommend = recomendar
  • series = série

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "What kind of movies do you like?" → Que tipo de filme você gosta?
  2. "I love imagining ___." → Adoro imaginar ___.
  3. "I go about ___ times a month." → Vou cerca de ___ vezes por mês.
  4. "It was okay. Not the best." → Estava ok. Não o melhor.
  5. "You should watch ___." → Você deveria assistir ___.

COMO RECOMENDAR EM INGLÊS:

  • "You should watch ___." → Você deveria assistir ___.
  • "I highly recommend ___." → Recomendo muito ___.
  • "You'd love ___." → Você adoraria ___.
  • "Don't miss ___." → Não perca ___.

CONVERSA 04 — VIDEO GAMES

Tema: Hobbies, jogos, lazer
Nível: Iniciante
Question words: What / How often / Where / Who / Why / When / Would

Q: What do you do for fun?
A: I like to play video games.

Q: How often do you play them?
A: I play them every weekend.

Q: Where do you play them?
A: I play them in my bedroom.

Q: Who do you play with?
A: I play with my older brother.

Q: Why do you like this game?
A: Because it has an amazing story.

Q: When did you buy it?
A: I bought it last Tuesday afternoon.

Q: Would you recommend it to me?
A: Yes, you would love it completely.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • video games = videogames / jogos eletrônicos
  • every weekend = todo fim de semana
  • bedroom = quarto
  • older brother = irmão mais velho
  • amazing story = história incrível
  • completely = completamente

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "What do you do for fun?" → O que você faz para se divertir?
  2. "I like to ___." → Gosto de ___.
  3. "I play with my ___." → Jogo com meu/minha ___.
  4. "Because it has an amazing ___." → Porque tem um/uma ___ incrível.
  5. "You would love it." → Você adoraria.

PRATIQUE:

  • What do you do for fun? → I like to ___.
  • How often do you ___? → I ___ every ___.
  • Why do you like ___? → Because it ___.

CONVERSA 05 — RESTAURANTE

Tema: Pedir comida, pagar, serviços
Nível: Iniciante
Question words: Can / Do / How about / When / Where / Can we

Q: Can I have a cheeseburger and fries?
A: Sure. Anything else?

Q: Do you serve sushi here?
A: Sorry, we don't have sushi.

Q: How about steak?
A: Yes, we do serve steaks.

Q: When will our food arrive?
A: It will arrive in 15 minutes.

Q: Where is the restroom located?
A: It is down the hallway.

Q: Can we have the bill, please?
A: Right. Yes, I will bring it now.

Q: Can we pay by card?
A: Sorry, we only accept cash.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • cheeseburger = hambúrguer com queijo
  • fries = batatas fritas
  • Anything else? = Mais alguma coisa?
  • serve = servir / ter no cardápio
  • restroom = banheiro (americano)
  • located = localizado
  • hallway = corredor
  • bill = conta
  • accept cash = aceitar dinheiro

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "Can I have ___?" → Posso ter ___? / Me traz ___.
  2. "Do you serve ___ here?" → Vocês servem ___ aqui?
  3. "It will arrive in ___ minutes." → Chegará em ___ minutos.
  4. "It is down the hallway." → É pelo corredor.
  5. "We only accept cash." → Só aceitamos dinheiro.

NO RESTAURANTE — FRASES ESSENCIAIS:

  • "Can I see the menu?" → Posso ver o cardápio?
  • "What do you recommend?" → O que você recomenda?
  • "Can we have the bill?" → Pode trazer a conta?
  • "Is service included?" → A gorjeta está incluída?

ERRO CLÁSSICO:
❌ "Give me a cheeseburger." (rude)
✓ "Can I have a cheeseburger, please?" (educado)
✓ "I'd like a cheeseburger, please." (mais formal)

CONVERSA 06 — CELULAR E TECNOLOGIA

Tema: Smartphones, tecnologia, compras online
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Question words: What / How long / Where / Why / How often / Can / When

Q: What phone do you have?
A: I have the latest iPhone model.

Q: How long does the battery last?
A: It lasts for a whole day.

Q: Where did you buy it?
A: I bought it online last week.

Q: Why is it so expensive?
A: It has an excellent camera system.

Q: How often do you change phones?
A: I change them every 2 years.

Q: Can it take photos underwater?
A: Yes, it is fully waterproof.

Q: When will you upgrade it again?
A: Probably in two or 3 years.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • latest model = modelo mais recente
  • battery = bateria
  • last = durar (tempo)
  • whole day = dia inteiro
  • camera system = sistema de câmera
  • waterproof = à prova d'água
  • upgrade = atualizar / trocar por modelo melhor

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "I have the latest ___." → Tenho o/a ___ mais recente.
  2. "It lasts for a whole day." → Dura o dia inteiro.
  3. "I bought it online." → Comprei online.
  4. "It is fully waterproof." → É totalmente à prova d'água.
  5. "Probably in ___ years." → Provavelmente em ___ anos.

COMO FALAR DE TECNOLOGIA:

  • "It has great features." → Tem ótimos recursos.
  • "The battery life is excellent." → A duração da bateria é excelente.
  • "It's worth the price." → Vale o preço.
  • "I'd highly recommend it." → Recomendo muito.

CONVERSA 07 — LIMPEZA DA CASA

Tema: Casa, limpeza, tarefas domésticas
Nível: Iniciante
Question words: Why / When / Where / How can / Should / What / How long

Q: Why is the kitchen so messy?
A: We cooked a big dinner yesterday.

Q: When will you clean it up?
A: I will clean it right now.

Q: Where is the vacuum cleaner?
A: It is in the hall closet.

Q: How can I help you clean?
A: You can wash the dirty dishes.

Q: Should we wash the windows today?
A: No, it will rain this afternoon.

Q: What did you do with the trash?
A: I put it outside already.

Q: How long will this take?
A: It will take 30 minutes.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • messy = bagunçado / sujo
  • clean up = limpar / arrumar
  • vacuum cleaner = aspirador de pó
  • hall closet = armário do corredor
  • dirty dishes = louça suja
  • trash = lixo
  • take (tempo) = levar (tempo)

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "Why is ___ so messy?" → Por que ___ está tão bagunçado?
  2. "I will clean it right now." → Vou limpar agora mesmo.
  3. "How can I help?" → Como posso ajudar?
  4. "You can ___." → Você pode ___.
  5. "It will take ___ minutes." → Vai levar ___ minutos.

TAREFAS DOMÉSTICAS EM INGLÊS:

  • do the dishes = lavar a louça
  • vacuum the floor = aspirar o chão
  • take out the trash = levar o lixo
  • do the laundry = lavar a roupa
  • make the bed = fazer a cama
  • clean the bathroom = limpar o banheiro

CONVERSA 08 — HOTEL

Tema: Hospedagem, check-in, regras do hotel
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Question words: Where / How much / What / When / How / Can / What time

Q: Where is the hotel located?
A: It is right next to the beach.

Q: How much does a night cost?
A: It costs $80 per night.

Q: What does the price include?
A: It includes breakfast and free Wi-Fi.

Q: When can we check in?
A: You can check in at 2:00 p.m.

Q: How can I pay for it?
A: You can pay in cash or by credit card.

Q: Can we bring our dog?
A: No, pets are not allowed here.

Q: What time is checkout?
A: Checkout is at 11 a.m.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • located = localizado / situado
  • right next to = bem ao lado de / pertinho de
  • per night = por noite
  • includes = inclui
  • check in = fazer check-in / se hospedar
  • pets = animais de estimação
  • allowed = permitido
  • checkout = check-out / saída

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "It is right next to ___." → Fica bem ao lado de ___.
  2. "How much does it cost per night?" → Quanto custa por noite?
  3. "What does the price include?" → O que o preço inclui?
  4. "Pets are not allowed." → Animais não são permitidos.
  5. "Checkout is at ___." → O checkout é às ___.

NO HOTEL — FRASES ESSENCIAIS:

  • "I have a reservation." → Tenho uma reserva.
  • "Can I get a room with a sea view?" → Posso ter um quarto com vista para o mar?
  • "Is breakfast included?" → O café da manhã está incluído?
  • "Can I have a late checkout?" → Posso fazer checkout mais tarde?

CONVERSA 09 — COZINHANDO

Tema: Cozinha, receitas, culinária
Nível: Iniciante
Question words: What / How / Why / When / Where / Can / Is

Q: What are you making for dinner?
A: I am making chicken pasta.

Q: How do you cook the chicken?
A: I fry it with some oil.

Q: Why do you add so much garlic?
A: Because garlic adds a great flavor.

Q: When should I boil the pasta?
A: Boil it when the water is hot.

Q: Where did you find this recipe?
A: I found it on the internet.

Q: Can you bake bread, too?
A: Yes, but it takes more time.

Q: Is the food ready yet?
A: Yes, let's eat right now.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • chicken pasta = macarrão com frango
  • fry = fritar
  • garlic = alho
  • flavor = sabor / sabor
  • boil = ferver / cozinhar em água
  • recipe = receita
  • bake = assar (no forno)
  • yet = ainda / já

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "What are you making?" → O que você está fazendo/cozinhando?
  2. "I fry it with some oil." → Frijo com um pouco de óleo.
  3. "Garlic adds a great flavor." → O alho dá um ótimo sabor.
  4. "It takes more time." → Leva mais tempo.
  5. "Let's eat right now." → Vamos comer agora mesmo.

MÉTODOS DE COZIMENTO:

  • fry = fritar
  • bake = assar (forno)
  • boil = ferver
  • grill = grelhar
  • steam = cozinhar no vapor
  • roast = assar (carne)

INGREDIENTES COMUNS:

  • garlic = alho
  • olive oil = azeite
  • salt and pepper = sal e pimenta
  • onion = cebola
  • herbs = ervas
  • spices = temperos

CONVERSA 10 — TRANSPORTE E DIREÇÕES

Tema: Metrô, ônibus, como chegar a algum lugar
Nível: Iniciante
Question words: Where / How / Can / How long / Where should / Is there / How often

Q: Where is the nearest metro station?
A: It's on Park Avenue.

Q: How do I get there?
A: Turn left and go straight ahead.

Q: Can I walk there from here?
A: Yes, it's 30 minutes on foot.

Q: How long will it take by bus?
A: It should take just around 7 minutes.

Q: Where should I get off?
A: Get off at the Central Park stop.

Q: Is there a bus stop nearby?
A: Yes, there's one on the next street.

Q: How often do the buses come?
A: They come every 15 minutes or so.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • nearest = mais próximo
  • metro station = estação de metrô
  • go straight ahead = siga em frente
  • on foot = a pé
  • get off = descer (ônibus/metrô)
  • stop = parada / ponto
  • nearby = perto / nas proximidades
  • every 15 minutes or so = a cada 15 minutos mais ou menos

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "Where is the nearest ___?" → Onde fica o/a ___ mais próximo/a?
  2. "Turn left and go straight." → Vire à esquerda e siga em frente.
  3. "It's ___ minutes on foot." → São ___ minutos a pé.
  4. "Get off at ___." → Desça em ___.
  5. "They come every ___ minutes." → Passam a cada ___ minutos.

DIREÇÕES — VOCABULÁRIO ESSENCIAL:

  • turn left = vire à esquerda
  • turn right = vire à direita
  • go straight = siga em frente
  • at the corner = na esquina
  • next to = ao lado de
  • across from = em frente a / do outro lado de
  • between = entre

CONVERSA 11 — TEMPO E CLIMA

Tema: Clima, previsão do tempo, o que vestir
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Question words: How's / How cold / Should / Will there / How will / How can / What should

Q: How's the weather?
A: It's cold and a bit cloudy.

Q: How cold is it there?
A: It's about 8 degrees.

Q: Should I bring an umbrella?
A: Yes, it might rain any time.

Q: Will there be thunder and lightning?
A: I can already hear the thunder.

Q: How will the weather be tomorrow?
A: It will probably be sunny and warm.

Q: How can you be sure?
A: I'm not sure. Just guessing.

Q: What should I wear tomorrow?
A: A light jacket should be enough.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • cloudy = nublado
  • umbrella = guarda-chuva
  • thunder = trovão
  • lightning = relâmpago
  • probably = provavelmente
  • sunny = ensolarado
  • light jacket = jaqueta leve
  • should be enough = deveria ser suficiente
  • just guessing = só chutando

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "It's cold and a bit cloudy." → Está frio e um pouco nublado.
  2. "It might rain any time." → Pode chover a qualquer momento.
  3. "It will probably be ___." → Provavelmente vai estar ___.
  4. "I'm not sure. Just guessing." → Não tenho certeza. Só chutando.
  5. "A ___ should be enough." → Um/Uma ___ deveria ser suficiente.

DESCREVENDO O CLIMA:

  • hot = quente / sunny = ensolarado
  • warm = morno / cloudy = nublado
  • cool = fresquinho / windy = ventoso
  • cold = frio / rainy = chuvoso
  • freezing = congelando / snowy = nevando
  • humid = úmido / dry = seco

CONVERSA 12 — VIAGEM E FÉRIAS

Tema: Destinos, experiências de viagem
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Question words: Where / How long / How / What / Was / Did / Would

Q: Where did you go last summer?
A: I went to Thailand.

Q: How long were you there?
A: I was there for two weeks.

Q: How did you get there?
A: I flew from New York.

Q: What did you do there?
A: I visited temples and beaches.

Q: What was the food like?
A: It was spicy but really delicious.

Q: Did you have any problems there?
A: Yes, I lost my phone once.

Q: Would you go back again?
A: Yes, absolutely. I loved it.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • last summer = no verão passado
  • flew = voei (passado de fly)
  • temples = templos
  • spicy = picante / apimentado
  • delicious = delicioso
  • lost my phone = perdi meu celular
  • absolutely = com certeza / absolutamente

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "Where did you go last summer?" → Onde você foi no verão passado?
  2. "I was there for ___ weeks." → Fiquei lá por ___ semanas.
  3. "I flew from ___." → Voei de ___.
  4. "What was the food like?" → Como era a comida?
  5. "Would you go back again?" → Você voltaria?
  6. "Yes, absolutely. I loved it." → Sim, com certeza. Amei.

FALANDO DE VIAGEM:

  • "The trip was amazing." → A viagem foi incrível.
  • "I'd highly recommend it." → Recomendo muito.
  • "The people were very friendly." → O povo era muito simpático.
  • "It's worth the trip." → Vale a viagem.

PERGUNTA ESPECIAL:
"What was ___ like?" → Como era ___? / Como foi ___?
Essa estrutura é muito usada e pouco ensinada!

  • "What was the food like?" → Como era a comida?
  • "What was the hotel like?" → Como era o hotel?
  • "What was he like?" → Como ele era?

CONVERSA 13 — APRENDENDO INGLÊS

Tema: Estudo de idiomas, dificuldades, progresso
Nível: Intermediário
Question words: Why / How long / How often / What / How / Can / Have

Q: Why do you want to learn English?
A: I need it for my job.

Q: How long have you been studying?
A: I've been studying for 2 years.

Q: How often do you practice?
A: I practice every day for an hour.

Q: What do you find most difficult?
A: I find speaking the most difficult.

Q: How do you practice speaking?
A: I watch English shows without subtitles.

Q: Can you speak well now?
A: I can speak fairly well.

Q: Have you taken any English tests?
A: Yes, I took the IELTS last year.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • need it for my job = preciso para o meu trabalho
  • been studying = tenho estudado (Present Perfect Continuous)
  • practice = praticar
  • find ___ difficult = achar ___ difícil
  • subtitles = legendas
  • fairly well = razoavelmente bem
  • IELTS = exame internacional de inglês

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "I need it for my job." → Preciso para o meu trabalho.
  2. "I've been studying for ___." → Estudo há ___.
  3. "I practice every day for ___." → Pratico todo dia por ___.
  4. "I find ___ the most difficult." → Acho ___ o mais difícil.
  5. "I can speak fairly well." → Consigo falar razoavelmente bem.

FALE SOBRE SEU INGLÊS:

  • Why do you want to learn English? → I want to ___ / I need it for ___.
  • How long have you been studying? → I've been studying for ___.
  • What do you find most difficult? → I find ___ the most difficult.
  • How do you practice? → I ___.

ADVÉRBIOS DE GRAU (para descrever seu nível):

  • fluently = fluentemente
  • fairly well = razoavelmente bem
  • a little / a bit = um pouco
  • not very well = não muito bem
  • barely = mal / quase não

CONVERSA 14 — CHEGANDO ATRASADO

Tema: Atraso, desculpas, trânsito, comprometimento
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Question words: Why / When / How / Will / How can / How / What if

Q: Why are you late?
A: I got stuck in traffic.

Q: When did you leave home?
A: I left home at 9 a.m.

Q: How did you come here?
A: I took the bus.

Q: Will you be late again?
A: No, I won't be late ever again.

Q: How can you assure me?
A: Well, I'll leave from home early.

Q: How early?
A: About 30 minutes early.

Q: What if you're late again?
A: You can punish me.

VOCABULÁRIO:

  • got stuck in traffic = fiquei preso no trânsito
  • leave home = sair de casa
  • took the bus = peguei o ônibus
  • ever again = nunca mais
  • assure = assegurar / garantir
  • punish = punir / castigar

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "I got stuck in traffic." → Fiquei preso no trânsito.
  2. "I took the bus." → Peguei o ônibus.
  3. "I won't ___ ever again." → Nunca mais vou ___.
  4. "I'll leave from home early." → Vou sair de casa cedo.
  5. "What if ___?" → E se ___?

DESCULPAS EM INGLÊS:

  • "I'm so sorry I'm late." → Sinto muito por estar atrasado.
  • "I got stuck in traffic." → Fiquei preso no trânsito.
  • "My bus was delayed." → Meu ônibus atrasou.
  • "I overslept." → Eu dormi demais.
  • "It won't happen again." → Não vai acontecer de novo.

EXPRESSÃO ESPECIAL:
"I got stuck in ___."

  • stuck in traffic = preso no trânsito
  • stuck in a meeting = preso em uma reunião
  • stuck at work = preso no trabalho
  • stuck in an elevator = preso no elevador

RESUMO DOS 14 TEMAS

01. Rotina de Trabalho   → What/How/When + horários
02. Cidade Natal         → Where/How/What + origem
03. Filmes               → What/Why/Who + preferências
04. Video Games          → What/How/Where/Who + hobbies
05. Restaurante          → Can/Do/When + serviços
06. Celular              → What/How/Where + tecnologia
07. Limpeza da Casa      → Why/When/Where + tarefas
08. Hotel                → Where/How much/What + hospedagem
09. Cozinhando           → What/How/Why + culinária
10. Transporte           → Where/How/Can + direções
11. Clima                → How/Should/Will + previsão
12. Viagem               → Where/How/What + experiências
13. Aprendendo Inglês    → Why/How/What + estudo
14. Chegando Atrasado    → Why/When/How + desculpas

SISTEMA 4 — INGLÊS EM CENA

Aprenda inglês com diálogos reais, humor e situações do dia a dia

Baseado no Top Notch — English for Today's World

MÓDULO 1 — 20 CENAS COM DIÁLOGO

Cada cena: diálogo original → vocabulário → frases-chave → o que aprender

CENA 01 — Apresentações na Agência de Viagens

Situação: Giorgio Moretti, um cantor italiano famoso, visita a agência de viagens Top Notch pela primeira vez.
Nível: Iniciante
Tema: Apresentações, profissões, nacionalidades

DIÁLOGO:

— You're from Italy?
— Yes, I am.
— Welcome to Top Notch Travel Agency. Let me introduce you to my staff.
— Marie, I'd like you to meet Giorgio.
— Oh, you already know him?
— It's very nice to meet you. What's your name?
— My name is Marie. Marie Léage.
— Very nice to meet you, Marie.
— Marie is our receptionist. She's from Paris.
— Mr. Moretti is a new client. He's from Italy.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • welcome to = bem-vindo a
  • let me introduce you to = deixa eu te apresentar a
  • staff = equipe / funcionários
  • I'd like you to meet = quero que você conheça
  • receptionist = recepcionista
  • client = cliente

FRASES-CHAVE (para usar no dia a dia):

  1. "I'd like you to meet ___." → Quero que você conheça ___.
  2. "She's from Paris." → Ela é de Paris.
  3. "He's a new client." → Ele é um novo cliente.
  4. "It's very nice to meet you." → É um prazer te conhecer.

O QUE APRENDER:

  • Como apresentar alguém formalmente: "I'd like you to meet ___"
  • Como dizer de onde alguém é: "She's from ___"
  • Como descrever a função de alguém: "She's our receptionist"
  • MACETE: "I'd like you to meet" é mais educado que "meet my friend"

ERROS CLÁSSICOS DO BRASILEIRO:

  • ❌ "I present you my friend" → ✓ "I'd like you to meet my friend"
  • ❌ "She is from the Paris" → ✓ "She's from Paris" (sem artigo com cidades)

CENA 02 — Conhecendo a Equipe

Situação: Giorgio é apresentado a cada membro da equipe — Cheryl, Bob e Paul.
Nível: Iniciante
Tema: Apresentações, apelidos, funções no trabalho

DIÁLOGO:

— This is Cheryl.
— Hello, Mr. Giorgio... I mean, Mr. Moretti.
— Please, call me Giorgio.
— Bob! Come meet Giorgio Moretti.
— Hey man, how are you? I'm Bob. But everyone calls me Roberto.
— Who calls you Roberto?
— I'm also a travel agent.
— And Paul is a tour guide.
— Goodbye! So long! It's nice to meet you, but I must be going.
— Toby! So long! It's nice to know you, but I'm traveling down.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • office manager = gerente de escritório
  • travel agent = agente de viagens
  • tour guide = guia de turismo
  • Please, call me ___ = Por favor, me chame de ___
  • everyone calls me = todo mundo me chama de
  • I must be going = preciso ir

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "Please, call me ___." → Por favor, me chame de ___.
  2. "Everyone calls me ___." → Todo mundo me chama de ___.
  3. "I must be going." → Preciso ir / Tenho que ir.
  4. "So long!" → Até mais! (informal, um pouco antiquado mas usado)

O QUE APRENDER:

  • Como pedir para alguém usar seu apelido ou primeiro nome
  • Profissões em inglês: travel agent, tour guide, office manager
  • "I must be going" — forma educada de se despedir no meio de conversa

CENA 03 — Ficha do Cliente

Situação: Marie preenche a ficha de Giorgio com suas informações pessoais.
Nível: Iniciante
Tema: Informações pessoais, estado civil, profissões

DIÁLOGO:

— Let's see... Name: Giorgio Moretti.
— Occupation?
— Singer. Famous singer.
— Great. And famous singer.
— Nationality: Italian.
— Age: 32.
— Married?
— No. Single.
— Phone number?
— This is my information.
— Everything okay?
— Come with me, Mr. Moretti.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • occupation = profissão / ocupação
  • nationality = nacionalidade
  • age = idade
  • married = casado
  • single = solteiro
  • phone number = número de telefone

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "What's your occupation?" → Qual é a sua profissão?
  2. "I'm single." → Sou solteiro/a.
  3. "I'm married." → Sou casado/a.
  4. "What's your phone number?" → Qual é o seu número de telefone?

COMPARAÇÕES ÚTEIS:

  • job = trabalho (informal)
  • occupation = profissão (formal, em formulários)
  • career = carreira (trajetória profissional)

CENA 04 — Saindo no Fim de Semana

Situação: O grupo discute o que fazer no fim de semana — cinema, rock, peça de teatro ou ópera.
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Tema: Lazer, preferências, expressões de opinião

DIÁLOGO:

— Do you guys want to go out this weekend?
— There's a great movie playing at the Glenwood.
— A rock concert sounds better to me.
— I'd love to see a play.
— How about an opera?
— Okay, there's a rock concert Saturday night at 8pm. Blue City is playing.
— Blue City! I love them!
— Sounds good.
— Not my style. I don't like rock.
— Okay, there's a play tonight at midnight at the 2nd Avenue Theater.
— It's called "Conversations with Food."
— Sounds great!
— At midnight? That's way past my bedtime. No thanks.
— Carmen is playing at the City Opera. 8pm.
— How much are the tickets?
— [shocked reaction] Whoa! Oh no way!
— Great, it's a movie then.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • sounds good = parece bom / soa bem
  • not my style = não é meu estilo
  • way past my bedtime = muito depois da minha hora de dormir
  • playing = em cartaz / tocando
  • How much are the tickets? = Quanto custam os ingressos?

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "A ___ sounds better to me." → ___ parece melhor para mim.
  2. "Not my style." → Não é meu estilo.
  3. "That's way past my bedtime!" → Isso é muito tarde para mim!
  4. "Sounds good." → Parece bom.
  5. "I'd love to see ___." → Eu adoraria ver ___.

O QUE APRENDER:

  • Como expressar preferência: "sounds better to me"
  • Como recusar educadamente: "not my style" / "no thanks"
  • "Way" como intensificador: "way past" = muito além de

CENA 05 — Como Chegar ao Cinema

Situação: Alguém pede direções para o Rose Cinema e recebe instruções confusas.
Nível: Iniciante-Intermediário
Tema: Dar e pedir direções

DIÁLOGO:

— Excuse me. I'm looking for the Rose Cinema.
— The Rose Cinema? Let's see... that's on the corner of Market Street and Park Street.
— Or is it Third and Grand? No, I think it's on Market between First and Second Avenue.
— Okay, so go around the corner, walk three blocks... no, five blocks to Harper Street.
— Turn left. Sorry, right.
— Go another two blocks — no, yes, two blocks — to 4th Avenue.
— Take a right. Walk about five blocks to Market Street.
— Go right again. Go straight two more blocks. The cinema is on your right.
— Uh... no. Sorry. Your left.
[another person walks up]
— You're looking for the Rose Cinema?
— Yes!
— Go across the street. It's right there.
— Thank you.
— And you're a tour guide?!

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • I'm looking for ___ = Estou procurando ___
  • on the corner of = na esquina de
  • between = entre
  • go around the corner = vire a esquina
  • walk ___ blocks = ande ___ quarteirões
  • turn left / right = vire à esquerda / direita
  • go straight = siga em frente
  • across the street = do outro lado da rua

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "I'm looking for ___." → Estou procurando ___.
  2. "It's on the corner of ___ and ___." → Fica na esquina de ___ com ___.
  3. "Go straight two blocks." → Siga em frente dois quarteirões.
  4. "Turn left at the light." → Vire à esquerda no sinal.
  5. "It's right there." → É bem ali.

HUMOR DA CENA:
A ironia é que o guia de turismo dá direções completamente confusas, e um estranho resolve tudo com uma frase simples. Lição: às vezes a resposta mais simples é a melhor!

CENA 06 — Fotos da Família

Situação: Bob estuda fotos da família de Cheryl para se preparar para conhecê-los.
Nível: Iniciante
Tema: Família, relações familiares, descrições

DIÁLOGO:

— That's your cousin Teddy. He's a waiter. He's single and he likes rock music.
— It's my brother Eddie. He's a doctor. He's got a wife and two kids. He likes classical music.
— How about this one?
— I don't know... a cousin? No. Your brother? No. An uncle?
— It's my Aunt Judy. Sorry, Mrs. Morris.
— She looks like your uncle.
— Tell me something about her.
— She's an architect. Married. Divorced. Two kids. Three kids. Four kids. Five kids. No kids.
— Only eight more.
— Here's an easy one.
— I don't know.
— It's my father.
— I know who your father is! Why are you showing me photos of your father?
— My family is coming in one hour. Now pay attention!
— Why do you have such a large family?
— It's not that large!
— Not that large? You have six brothers and sisters, 14 aunts and uncles, who knows how many cousins, nieces and nephews.
— I'd say that's a large family.
— They're not all coming over.
— No? Just 18 of them.
— I'm sorry, honey. I just want them to like you.
— Calm down. It's okay. You're doing fine.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • cousin = primo/prima
  • brother / sister = irmão / irmã
  • aunt / uncle = tia / tio
  • niece / nephew = sobrinha / sobrinho
  • single = solteiro
  • divorced = divorciado
  • architect = arquiteto
  • He's got a wife and two kids = Ele tem uma esposa e dois filhos

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "He's got a wife and two kids." → Ele tem esposa e dois filhos.
  2. "She's an architect." → Ela é arquiteta.
  3. "I just want them to like you." → Só quero que eles gostem de você.
  4. "Calm down. You're doing fine." → Calma. Você está indo bem.

FAMÍLIA EM INGLÊS — GUIA RÁPIDO:

  • parents = pais (pai + mãe)
  • siblings = irmãos (irmão + irmã)
  • in-laws = sogros / cunhados
  • grandparents = avós
  • grandchildren = netos

CENA 07 — Barganhando pela Câmera

Situação: Paul tenta vender sua câmera digital usada e Bob e Cheryl tentam barganhar.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Negociação, preços, barganhar

DIÁLOGO:

— Hey, you want to sell me this digital camera?
— The best digital camera money can buy!
— Why are you selling it?
— Cheryl gave me another one for my birthday.
— How much do you want?
— $250.
— Wow, that's a great price... but that's more than I want to pay.
— I can give you $200 for it.
— No, I need at least $245.
— Sorry, all I have is $210.
— I could go as low as $230. But that's it.
— Sorry. Thanks anyway.
[Later]
— You almost bought that camera yesterday for $300!
— You don't know how to bargain, do you?
— Of course I know how to bargain!
— You don't know how to bargain. You could buy that camera for $230!
— All right, you can have it for $225.
— $220.
— $224.
— $221.
— $223.
— $222. Not a dollar more.
— I'm not selling this for less than $223.
— Here's $1. Now you both get what you want.
— It's a deal!

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • bargain = barganhar / pechinchar
  • How much do you want? = Quanto você quer?
  • at least = pelo menos
  • I could go as low as = posso baixar até
  • Thanks anyway = obrigado mesmo assim
  • It's a deal! = Fechado! / É um acordo!
  • Not a dollar more = nem um centavo a mais

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "How much do you want for it?" → Quanto você quer por isso?
  2. "That's more than I want to pay." → Isso é mais do que quero pagar.
  3. "I could go as low as ___." → Posso baixar até ___.
  4. "It's a deal!" → Fechado!
  5. "Not a dollar more." → Nem um centavo a mais.

MACETES DE NEGOCIAÇÃO:

  • "Can you do better?" = Você consegue um preço melhor?
  • "That's my final offer." = Essa é minha oferta final.
  • "Meet me in the middle." = Vamos no meio-termo.

CENA 08 — A Conta do Restaurante

Situação: Bob e Paul discutem sobre quanto deixar de gorjeta.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Restaurante, gorjeta, matemática cotidiana

DIÁLOGO:

— I'll ask for the check.
— $5? That's not enough!
— Sure it is.
— The bill was $50. That's only 10%.
— Didn't you like the food?
— It was good.
— Was there a problem with the service?
— No.
— Then you need to leave at least 15%.
— No, I don't.
— We come here all the time! The waitress gives us great service because we usually tip well.
— I always leave 10%.
— Look, I'm paying tonight, so I get to decide how much to tip.
— Oh! All right. Hey, isn't that Mr. Evans over there?
— Where?
— Never mind, it's someone else.
— Shall we go?

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • check = conta (nos EUA) / bill = conta (inglês britânico)
  • tip = gorjeta
  • service = serviço / atendimento
  • at least = pelo menos
  • I get to decide = cabe a mim decidir
  • Never mind = deixa pra lá / não importa
  • Shall we go? = Vamos?

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "Can we get the check, please?" → Pode trazer a conta, por favor?
  2. "Was there a problem with the service?" → Teve algum problema com o serviço?
  3. "I get to decide." → Cabe a mim decidir.
  4. "Never mind." → Deixa pra lá.
  5. "Shall we go?" → Vamos?

CULTURA AMERICANA — GORJETA:

  • 15% = mínimo aceitável
  • 20% = bom serviço
  • 25%+ = serviço excelente
  • Não dar gorjeta = insulto grave nos EUA

CENA 09 — Escolhendo Roupas para a Festa

Situação: Marie e Cheryl pedem a opinião de Bob sobre o que vestir para a festa.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Roupas, opiniões, preferências

DIÁLOGO:

— Bob, what do you think of our new clothes for the party?
— There's a party tomorrow?
— It's Mr. Evans's birthday! Remember? You're going.
— Okay. So tell us what you think of our new clothes.
— All those clothes are for one party?
— No, we have to decide what to wear.
— What do you think of these blouses?
— They're very flattering.
— Which one do you like more?
— What do you mean, "which one"? Which one do you prefer?
— I like them both the same.
— No, you don't. You're just saying that. You need to have an opinion. You have to choose.
— No, no, no. I'm not doing that.
— Bob, please help us decide what to wear.
— Okay. Which skirt do you like — the red one?
— Great! That's not so hard, is it?
— Which shoes look better?
— Those.
— Which sweater do you prefer?
— I like the purple one.
— Bob! You like Marie's clothes more than mine!
— No, I don't! That's not true!
— Then which dress do you prefer?
— That one.
— This is Marie's dress too!
— I like your clothes. I like Marie's clothes. I like everything. I like all dresses and all sweaters and all skirts and all shoes.
— Who asked you anyway?

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • flattering = que fica bem / favorecedor
  • which one = qual deles
  • prefer = preferir
  • sweater = suéter / moletom
  • skirt = saia
  • blouse = blusa

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "What do you think of ___?" → O que você acha de ___?
  2. "Which one do you prefer?" → Qual você prefere?
  3. "I like them both the same." → Gosto dos dois igualmente.
  4. "You need to have an opinion." → Você precisa ter uma opinião.
  5. "Who asked you anyway?" → Quem perguntou pra você?

CENA 10 — O Dia de Bob Melhorar o Visual

Situação: Cheryl e Marie convencem Bob a se cuidar mais — manicure, cabelo, cuidados com a pele.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Aparência pessoal, cuidados, vocabulário de beleza

DIÁLOGO:

— Cheryl, your hair looks gorgeous!
— Thank you! I have a new shampoo. "Bright and Clean."
— Don't you use any skin care products? Body lotion or skin cream?
— No. Should I?
— If you want your skin to stay young and healthy.
— Do you use any conditioner?
— That's for women!
— Lots of men use it too!
— Really? Sure! Women like men who take care of their appearance.
— Really? Okay. What else should I do? You don't want me to wear makeup, do you?
— Lipstick? Mascara? Eye shadow? No. But how about a manicure?
— Look at your nails — they're a mess! Men get manicures.
— Many do, yes. We can give you one right here.
— Really? Piece of cake!
— Well, okay.
— Great! Then we can talk about your haircut, facial and face lift.
— What?!

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • gorgeous = lindo / deslumbrante
  • shampoo = xampu
  • skin care products = produtos de cuidado com a pele
  • body lotion = loção corporal
  • conditioner = condicionador
  • manicure = manicure
  • facial = limpeza de pele
  • face lift = cirurgia de levantamento facial
  • piece of cake = moleza / fácil
  • they're a mess = estão uma bagunça

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "Your hair looks gorgeous!" → Seu cabelo está lindo!
  2. "Piece of cake!" → Moleza! / Fácil!
  3. "They're a mess." → Estão uma bagunça.
  4. "Take care of your appearance." → Cuide da sua aparência.
  5. "What else should I do?" → O que mais devo fazer?

CENA 11 — A Impressora Quebrada

Situação: A equipe precisa imprimir ingressos urgentes mas a impressora está com problemas.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Escritório, tecnologia, urgência

DIÁLOGO:

— Where are the tickets? They're printing.
— Mr. Evans needs them right now! The client is coming in 5 minutes!
— This printer is driving me crazy! It's so slow!
— Try blowing on it.
— What?! Really?
— Try it. Now tap the sides. Just try it.
— Now rub this side gently.
— Does this really work?
[Later]
— The client's coming in 1 minute. The printer's a little slow today.
— Okay, stop! Don't come near this printer!
— What?
— You know machines don't work when you're around.
— That's not true!
— Is your laptop working? No.
— Is your cell phone working? No.
— Is your PDA working? No.
— But stay away!
— The client is here. Where are the tickets?
— Right here, sir.
— There are only nine. Where's the last one?
— Right here, sir.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • driving me crazy = me deixando louco
  • tap the sides = bata nas laterais
  • gently = suavemente / delicadamente
  • stay away = fique longe / não se aproxime
  • slow = lento
  • last one = último

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "This is driving me crazy!" → Isso está me deixando louco!
  2. "Stay away!" → Fique longe! / Não se aproxime!
  3. "We need it right now." → Precisamos agora mesmo.
  4. "The client is here." → O cliente chegou.
  5. "It's a little slow today." → Está um pouco lento hoje.

HUMOR DA CENA:
Bob parece fazer as máquinas pararem de funcionar. É uma piada sobre "aquela pessoa que estraga tudo que toca" — muito relatable!

CENA 12 — No Restaurante — Pedido Complicado

Situação: Um cliente difícil faz pedidos muito específicos e cheios de restrições.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Restaurante, pedidos, restrições alimentares

DIÁLOGO:

— Are you ready to order?
— I'm in the mood for lamb, but the sauce looks too fatty. Could I order the lamb without the sauce?
— Sure. What does it come with?
— French fries.
— I don't like fried food. Could I have a grilled vegetable instead?
— I think we have grilled peppers.
— Perfect. Would you like to start with an appetizer?
— Is there oil on the tomato salad?
— There's a lot of olive oil, yes.
— Could I get it without the oil?
— But it won't taste very good.
— Then I'll just have a mixed green salad.
— And you?
— I'm sorry, I have another question. Is there salt on the lamb? It's cooked with salt and pepper.
— I don't want a lot of salt. I think I'll have the fish instead.
— What's in the sauce?
— Lemon, butter, milk.
— Oh, that's too much dairy. Maybe I'll have a large salad for my entrée.
— No appetizer?
— What's in the salad?
— Lettuce, carrots, peppers, onions, eggs.
— Oh, no egg, please.
— Salad, no egg.
— Anything to drink?
— Just water, please.
— And for you?
— I'll have the special.
— Could I ask you another question?
— No.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • I'm in the mood for = estou com vontade de
  • fatty = gorduroso
  • fried = frito
  • grilled = grelhado
  • appetizer = entrada / aperitivo
  • entrée = prato principal
  • dairy = laticínios
  • What does it come with? = O que vem junto?

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "I'm in the mood for ___." → Estou com vontade de ___.
  2. "Could I order ___ without ___?" → Posso pedir ___ sem ___?
  3. "What does it come with?" → O que vem junto?
  4. "Could I have ___ instead?" → Posso ter ___ em vez disso?
  5. "Just water, please." → Só água, por favor.

CENA 13 — A Férias Perfeita e a Péssima

Situação: O Sr. Rasheed volta de uma terrível viagem mas está feliz por ter encontrado alguém especial.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Viagem, adjetivos, contraste, romance

DIÁLOGO:

— Welcome back! How's Los Angeles?
— The vacation was wonderful!
— Was your flight okay?
— No, pretty bad actually. It was so bumpy. Very scary.
— Did you have nice weather?
— No, the weather was terrible. Very rainy. I never saw the sun.
— So what did you do?
— I stayed inside.
— Was the hotel room nice?
— The room was fine, but it was right next to the cafe and the music was very loud. I didn't sleep much.
— I'll bet the food was great!
— No, it was too salty, and the waiters were very unfriendly.
— Did you go shopping?
— A little. Until someone stole my wallet.
— Was the flight home okay?
— Actually, they cancelled my flight. I had to stay for two more days.
— That's terrible! But Mr. Rasheed... you said your vacation was wonderful!
— Ah, yes, I did. And it was wonderful!
— I met a very nice person. A woman. Her name is Bazar. She's from Lebanon, just like me. But she lives here.
— I'm seeing her tonight.
— So yes... it was a wonderful vacation.

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • bumpy = turbulento / com solavancos
  • scary = assustador
  • salty = salgado
  • unfriendly = antipático / grosseiro
  • stole my wallet = roubou minha carteira

— cancelled = cancelado

  • I'm seeing her = estou saindo com ela / vou encontrá-la

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "It was so bumpy." → Foi tão turbulento.
  2. "The weather was terrible." → O tempo estava terrível.
  3. "I didn't sleep much." → Não dormi muito.
  4. "I'll bet ___." → Aposto que ___.
  5. "I'm seeing her tonight." → Vou encontrá-la esta noite.

LIÇÃO DA CENA:
Tudo de ruim pode ser compensado por algo especial. E como descrever uma viagem com adjetivos fortes: terrible, wonderful, scary, unfriendly, salty.

CENA 14 — A Safari Confusa

Situação: Cheryl planeja o safari da Sra. Batty no Botswana, com meios de transporte cada vez mais inusitados.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Transporte, viagem, preposições de lugar

DIÁLOGO:

— In Johannesburg, you should take a taxi or a limo to your hotel.
— The next day you could fly or take a train to Francistown in Botswana.
— Is it an express train?
— Yes.
— I'll take the train. I'd like to see the country.
— Then you can take a small plane or a bus to the Okavango Delta.
— How small is the airplane?
— It's pretty small.
— I'll take the bus. Is it an express bus?
— I think so.
— When you get to Maun, you're going to be taking a boat to your hotel.
— A boat?
— The hotel is on an island.
— When you get to the island, a man with a donkey can take your luggage to the hotel.
— A donkey?
— There are no cars on the island.
— Is it an express donkey?
— I think it's probably a local donkey.
— Of course, if you don't want the donkey, you could take a small plane. It goes straight to the hotel.
— I think I should take the donkey. Donkeys never have mechanical problems, right?

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • safari = safári

— limo = limusine

  • express train = trem expresso
  • local bus = ônibus local (faz todas as paradas)
  • island = ilha
  • luggage = bagagem
  • donkey = burro / jumento
  • mechanical problems = problemas mecânicos

FRASES-CHAVE:

  1. "You should take a taxi." → Você deveria pegar um táxi.
  2. "You could fly or take a train." → Você pode voar ou pegar um trem.
  3. "How small is the airplane?" → Qual o tamanho do avião?
  4. "There are no cars on the island." → Não há carros na ilha.
  5. "It goes straight to the hotel." → Vai direto para o hotel.

HUMOR DA CENA:
A progressão dos meios de transporte — avião → trem → barco → burro — é hilária. E a pergunta "Is it an express donkey?" é clássica!

CENA 15 — Problemas no Escritório com Tecnologia

Situação: Todos pedem ajuda de Bob com problemas de tecnologia.
Nível: Intermediário
Tema: Tecnologia, computadores, pedidos de ajuda

DIÁLOGO:

— Bob, can you help me with something?
— Sure.
— I'm trying to print a file but the printer won't work.
— Push the green button on the printer.
— Why?
— To turn it on. It won't print unless it's on.
— Oh right. Silly me. Thank you.
[Next person]
— Hey Bob, my laptop crashed and I can't get it to do anything.
— Stick this here.
— Why?
— To restart the computer.
— Are you sure? Okay. Thanks.
[Next person]
— Bob, somebody sent me an email but I think it has a virus.
— Don't open the attachment. Click on the "No Virus" icon on the toolbar.
— Why?
— To clean the computer and stop the virus.
— Thanks, Bob.
[Last person]
— Bob, can I ask you another question?
— I'm sorry, but I can't get any work done with all these questions! I have some very important stuff I need to finish right now.
[Game over sound]
— Game over?
— Very important stuff.
— Game over?
— Game. How can I help?

VOCABULÁRIO DA CENA:

  • printer = impressora
  • green button = botão verde
